If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = q.batchPool[:batches-1]\n1486: \t\treturn batch\n1487: \t}\n1488: \treturn make([]timeSeries, 0, capacity)\n1489: }\n1490: \n1491: func (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n1492: \tdefer func() {\n1493: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1494: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \t}()\n1497: \n1498: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1499: \tsymbolTable := writev2.NewSymbolTable()\n1500: \n1501: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4@ba16cf5a7437eb3b6b71b74557b7a67e1975ad0f/-/blob/storage/remote/queue_manager.go%3FL1300-1500"}}}

Let me look at the `stop()` function more carefully and understand the race condition. The issue is in the resharding process. Let me trace through:\n\n1. `reshardLoop()` receives a signal to reshard with a new number of shards\n2. It calls `t.shards.stop()` which:\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel  \n   - Calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on all queues\n3. Then it calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` to create new shards\n\nThe problem mentioned in the issue is that during resharding, some shards might stall. Looking at the enqueue function:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n    s.mtx.RLock()\n    defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n    shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n    select {\n    case <-s.softShutdown:\n        return false\n    default:\n        appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n        ...\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe issue is:\n1. When `softShutdown` is closed, the select statement immediately returns false\n2. This causes the Append() caller to keep retrying with exponential backoff\n3. Meanwhile, the `stop()` function is waiting for all samples to flush\n\nBut wait, there's a deeper issue. When `stop()` is called:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) stop() {\n    // Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n    // to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n    // We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n    // RLock here.\n    s.mtx.RLock()\n    close(s.softShutdown)  // <-- This closes the channel\n    s.mtx.RUnlock()\n\n    // Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n    // also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n    // send on closed channel.\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n    for _, queue := range s.queues {\n        go queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n    }\n    select {\n    case <-s.done:\n```\n\nThe strategy here is to first close `softShutdown` with only a read lock, unblocking any pending enqueue operations. Then it acquires the write lock to safely call `FlushAndShutdown()` on each queue and wait for completion.\n\nHowever, there's a potential race condition: a thread might call `Append()`, get queued successfully, then on its next iteration call `enqueue()` which reads the closed `softShutdown` channel and returns false before the data is actually sent. The queued data could be lost if the flush doesn't capture it in Let me trace the race condition:\n\n## The Root Cause:\n\nLooking at the code, the problem is in the `enqueue()` function at line 1316-1341. The issue is that there's a race condition between the `softShutdown` channel being closed and samples being enqueued:\n\n1. **Thread 1 (reshardLoop)**: Calls `t.shards.stop()`:\n   - Line 1275: `close(s.softShutdown)` - This closes the softShutdown channel\n   - Line 1281-1285: Takes write lock and calls `queue.FlushAndShutdown()` for all queues\n   - Line 1286-1289: Waits for queues to flush or timeout\n\n2. **Thread 2 (Append goroutine)**: Calls `Append()` -> tries to call `enqueue()`:\n   - Line 1313: Takes RLock\n   - Line 1315: Calculates shard\n   - Line 1316-1318: Checks `softShutdown`\n   - **RACE CONDITION**: After RLock is released (line 1314 defer), but before the select statement is evaluated, `softShutdown` might be closed\n\nWait, let me think about this more carefully. The RLock is held during the select statement. So the race is:\n\n1. Append thread calls enqueue(), acquires RLock\n2. Meanwhile, reshardLoop() is waiting to acquire the write lock after closing softShutdown\n3. The select statement in enqueue() checks softShutdown - it's still open\n4. The Append() is added to the queue successfully\n5. The enqueue() returns true\n6. The RLock is released\n7. NOW the reshardLoop() gets the write lock\n8. BUT: The data was already enqueued and the pending metrics were incremented (line 1326)\n\n\n9. The queue gets stopped and flushed, but the pendingSamples counter is now inconsistent since samples arrived during the shutdown window\n\nThe real problem is the gap between closing softShutdown at line 1275 and acquiring the write lock at line 1281. During this window, new samples can still be enqueued because the RLock doesn't prevent the write lock from being acquired—it just delays it. Once the write lock is taken, the queue is flushed, but any samples that snuck in during that gap create a mismatch between what was actually queued and what the metrics report.\n\nLooking at FlushAndShutdown more carefully, it loops calling tryEnqueueingBatch until the batch is empty, sleeping between attempts. But tryEnqueueingBatch only sends if there's data—if the batchQueue channel is full (default case), it returns true to keep trying. The issue is that this flush process doesn't account for samples that might arrive after softShutdown closes but before the write lock is fully acquired and the flush completes.\n\nDuring resharding, when softShutdown closes, enqueue() immediately returns false. Callers retry with backoff, but if the new shards haven't started accepting data yet, those retries fail repeatedly. Samples accumulate in the queue, and once capacity is exceeded, the whole system can deadlock because there's nowhere for new data to go.\n\nThe real problem emerges from the resharding logs: after transitioning from 4 to 6 shards, some of those new shards end up with pending samples that never get flushed. The metrics show samples_pending stuck above zero with no forward progress, indicating the samples are trapped in the queue rather than being transmitted.\n\nLooking at the reshardLoop implementation, when the shard count changes, the old shards are stopped and new ones are started with different queue sizes. But here's where it breaks: samples that were assigned to shard positions based on the old shard count (4 shards) get reassigned based on the new count (6 shards). A sample that belonged to shard 2 under the 4-shard configuration might now belong to shard 4 under the 6-shard configuration. If those samples are already queued in the old shard when the transition happens, they could end up orphaned—stuck in a queue that's no longer being processed, or assigned to a new shard that never receives them because the routing logic has changed.\n\nThe real vulnerability appears to be in the enqueue function's timing. When a sample tries to enqueue during the resharding window, it calculates which shard to use based on the current shard count at that moment. If the softShutdown signal closes while samples are in flight, they get rejected from the old shard but then retry using stale shard calculations, potentially missing the new shard entirely.\n\nLooking more carefully at the actual code flow: once softShutdown closes, every enqueue call immediately returns false without even attempting to append. This means incoming samples get rejected outright. The queues should drain through FlushAndShutdown, but if new samples arrive after the shutdown signal but before the replacement shards are ready, they have nowhere to go—they're blocked from the old shards yet can't reach the new ones.\n\nThe critical window is between stop() closing softShutdown and start() bringing up the new shards. Any samples that arrive during this gap will be rejected, then retry with backoff. If the new shard startup is delayed or the timing aligns poorly, those samples risk being dropped entirely rather than successfully enqueued.\n\nThe solution involves keeping softShutdown open through the transition, or ensuring new queues are ready to accept samples before the old ones shut down completely. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01XSepZUw6Cq8HWjyZoDSuJd","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01UFaTWRYZMTpFJGTojTicCR","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe remote-write queue resharding failure is caused by a race condition between the old shards being stopped and new shards being started. When resharding occurs, the `softShutdown` channel is closed to prevent new enqueues, but this creates a window where in-flight samples cannot be enqueued to either old or new shards, causing samples to accumulate with metrics showing `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at values greater than zero.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1184-1199` (reshardLoop) and `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1269-1305` (stop function)\n\n**Specific Issue:** The resharding mechanism has a critical race condition in the state transition:\n\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n    for {\n        select {\n        case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n            t.shards.stop()      // Line 1193: Closes softShutdown\n            t.shards.start(numShards)  // Line 1194: Creates new shards\n```\n\nWhen `stop()` is called:\n1. Line 1275: `close(s.softShutdown)` immediately closes the channel\n2. Lines 1281-1285: The function takes a write lock and calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on all queues\n3. Lines 1286-1290: Waits up to `flushDeadline` for graceful shutdown\n\n**The Race Condition:**\n\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n    s.mtx.RLock()\n    defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n    shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n    select {\n    case <-s.softShutdown:    // Line 1317: After softShutdown is closed,\n        return false           // ALL future enqueues immediately return false\n    default:\n        appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n```\n\n**Timeline of Failure:**\n\n1. **T0**: `updateShardsLoop()` determines resharding is needed, sends signal on `reshardChan`\n2. **T1**: `reshardLoop()` receives signal and calls `t.shards.stop()`\n3. **T2**: `stop()` closes `softShutdown` channel at line 1275\n4. **T3**: In-flight `Append()` calls from TSDB try to `enqueue()`:\n   - The `select` statement on line 1316 immediately reads from closed `softShutdown`\n   - `enqueue()` returns `false` without attempting to queue the sample\n   - The `Append()` caller retries with exponential backoff (see line 748)\n5. **T4**: `stop()` acquires write lock and calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on old queues\n6. **T5**: **Critical Window**: Old shards are being flushed, but new shards haven't started yet\n   - Any samples trying to enqueue will fail\n   - The retry loop in `Append()` continues with backoff\n7. **T6**: `start()` creates new shards and begins accepting samples\n8. **T7**: Retrying `Append()` calls finally succeed\n\n**Problem:** If the retry loop encounters max backoff or times out before new shards are ready, or if samples experience multiple failed enqueues, they may be dropped due to age limits or backoff exhaustion (see line 706-708 in the `Append()` function).\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n1. **Resharding Loop** (`queue_manager.go:1184-1199`):\n   - Shows sequential `stop()` -> `start()` transition\n   - No synchronization between old shards being fully shutdown and new shards accepting samples\n\n2. **Stop Function** (`queue_manager.go:1269-1305`):\n   - Line 1275: `close(s.softShutdown)` - immediately blocks all enqueues\n   - Line 1281: Write lock only taken AFTER softShutdown is closed\n   - Race window exists between line 1275 and 1281\n\n3. **Enqueue Function** (`queue_manager.go:1312-1341`):\n   - Line 1316-1318: Select statement on closed channel immediately returns false\n   - Line 1317: `case <-s.softShutdown:` - reading from closed channel always succeeds\n   - No attempt to enqueue when softShutdown is closed\n\n4. **Append Function** (`queue_manager.go:700-758`):\n   - Line 706-708: Samples older than `SampleAgeLimit` are dropped\n   - Line 729-755: Exponential backoff retry loop with max backoff\n   - If backoff exceeds max before new shards start, enqueue attempts stop\n\n5. **CHANGELOG References**:\n   - Line 1457: \"BUGFIX Remote Write: Fixed blocked resharding edge case. #7122\"\n   - Line 1572: \"BUGFIX Remote write: do not reshard when unable to send samples. #6111\"\n\n### Metrics Confirming Issue\n\nThe metric `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` will show:\n- Value > 0 after resharding completes\n- Sustained stall with no progress (samples not being flushed)\n- Metrics would indicate samples stuck in queues during the resharding window\n\n### Why It's Intermittent\n\nThe issue is **timing-dependent and appears intermittent** because:\n\n1. **Target discovery timing**: When targets are added/removed, it takes time for metrics to flow through the system. The timing of when these metrics hit the queue during resharding determines if they're lost.\n\n2. **Load characteristics**:\n   - High load = more samples in flight = higher chance of hitting the race window\n   - Low load = fewer samples in flight = may not encounter the condition\n   - Specific metric patterns matter\n\n3. **System responsiveness**:\n   - Fast systems: New shards start quickly, minimizing the race window\n   - Slow systems: Larger window, higher probability of sample loss\n\n4. **Backoff timing**: Whether retry backoff aligns with the stop/start window affects whether samples are successfully requeued\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**:\n   - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` - orchestrates reshard\n   - `QueueManager.updateShardsLoop()` - triggers reshard decision\n   - `shards.stop()` - initiates shutdown\n   - `shards.start()` - creates new shards\n   - `shards.enqueue()` - attempts to queue samples\n\n2. **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - queue operations**:\n   - `queue.FlushAndShutdown()` - flushing during stop\n   - `queue.Append()` - initial queueing attempt\n\n3. **Metrics affected**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - will show non-zero stuck values\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - if samples exceed age limit\n\n4. **Related test file**:\n   - `storage/remote/queue_manager_test.go` - contains resharding test scenarios\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix should ensure samples in-flight during resharding can reach either old or new shards by:\n\n1. **Option A: Synchronous State Transition** - Don't close `softShutdown` until new shards are ready to accept samples:\n   - Create new shards first\n   - Only then close old shards' `softShutdown`\n   - This ensures a continuous path for samples\n\n2. **Option B: Atomic Shard Swap** - Use an atomic swap of the shards pointer:\n   - Create new shards and have them ready\n   - Atomically update the shard pointer\n   - Allow `enqueue()` to try a configurable number of times with the old shard count\n   - This maintains backward compatibility with in-flight calculations\n\n3. **Option C: Quiescing Before Resharding** - Enhanced shouldReshard check:\n   - Implement a pre-resharding quiesce period where no new enqueues are accepted\n   - Wait until all pending samples are flushed\n   - Then perform resharding with no in-flight samples\n   - Matches the intent of PR #6111 (\"do not reshard when unable to send samples\")\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this root cause in production, check for:\n\n1. **Logs showing sequential resharding**:\n   ```\n   msg=\"Remote storage resharding\" from=4 to=6\n   msg=\"Resharding done\" numShards=6\n   ```\n   followed by pending samples metric stuck at non-zero\n\n2. **Metrics queries**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{job=\"prometheus\"}` - should return to 0 eventually\n   - `increase(prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total[5m])` - check for spikes during resharding\n\n3. **Trace sampling**:\n   - Enable debug logging for queue manager\n   - Look for patterns of `case <-s.softShutdown: return false` in enqueue attempts\n   - Correlate with resharding log messages\n\n4. **Timing analysis**:\n   - Measure time between \"resharding from X to Y\" log and \"resharding done\"\n   - Correlate with target discovery events from scrape manager\n   - Check if delays in new shard startup correlate with sample loss\n\n## Additional Notes\n\nThe CHANGELOG entry for PR #7122 (\"Fixed blocked resharding edge case\") suggests this issue was identified and partially addressed, but the current code still exhibits the race condition. The fix may have addressed one manifestation (completely blocked resharding) but not the more subtle case of partial sample loss during the transition window.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":138,"cache_read_input_tokens":77617,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":138},"output_tokens":6,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"11ff0f7b-d70e-4455-9dfb-f42cccdccd53","uuid":"16c8a81a-dd56-4c52-9e8e-bf565e660540"}
